data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Romanian_People%27s_Salvation_Cathedral_Bukarest_7.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Romanian_People%27s_Salvation_Cathedral" title="Romanian People&#39;s Salvation Cathedral">Romanian People\'s Salvation Cathedral</a> (under construction) will be the seat of the Romanian patriarch</div></div></div>\n<p>Below is a list of the 14 (15) autocephalous Orthodox churches, all of which are titled equal to each other, but the Ecumenical Patriarchate is titled <i>first among equals</i>. Based on these definitions, the list is in their order of precedence and alphabetical order where necessary, with constituent autonomous churches and exarchates. The liturgical title of the primate is listed in italics. The communion:\n</p>\n<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarchate_of_Constantinople" title="Ecumenical Patriarchate of Constantinople">Ecumenical Patriarchate of Constantinople</a></b> (<i>Archbishop of Constantinople-New Rome and <a href="/wiki/Primus_inter_pares" title="Primus inter pares">First Among Equals</a> Patriarch</i>)\n<ul><li>Autonomous <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Orthodox_Church" title="Finnish Orthodox Church">Orthodox Church of Finland</a> (<i>Archbishop of Helsinki and All Finland</i>, formerly <i>Archbishop of Karelia and All Finland</i>)</li>\n<li>Self-governing Orthodox <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Crete" title="Church of Crete">Church of Crete</a> (<i>Archbishop of Crete</i>)</li>\n<li>Self-governing Monastic Community of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Athos" title="Mount Athos">Mount Athos</a></li>\n<li>Self-governing <a href="/wiki/Korean_Orthodox_Church" title="Korean Orthodox Church">Orthodox Church of Korea</a> (<i>Metropolitan of Seoul and all Korea</i>)</li></ul></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Patriarchate_of_Alexandria_and_all_Africa" title="Greek Orthodox Patriarchate of Alexandria and all Africa">Patriarchate of Alexandria</a></b> (<i>His Most Divine Beatitude the Pope and Patriarch of the Great City of <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pentapolis_(North_Africa)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentapolis (North Africa)">Pentapolis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, all the land of <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, and all <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, Father of Fathers, Shepherd of Shepherds, Prelate of Prelates, Thirteenth of the <a href="/wiki/Apostle_(Christian)" class="mw-redirect" title="Apostle (Christian)">Apostles</a>, and Judge of the <a href="/wiki/%C5%92cumene" class="mw-redirect" title="\xc5\x92cumene">\xc5\x92cumene</a></i>)</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Church_of_Antioch" title="Greek Orthodox Church of Antioch">Patriarchate of Antioch</a></b> (<i>Patriarch of Antioch and all the East</i>)\n<ul><li>Self-governing <a href="/wiki/Antiochian_Orthodox_Christian_Archdiocese_of_North_America" title="Antiochian Orthodox Christian Archdiocese of North America">Antiochian Orthodox Christian Archdiocese of North America</a> (<i>Archbishop of New York and Metropolitan of All North America</i>)</li></ul></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Church_of_Jerusalem" title="Greek Orthodox Church of Jerusalem">Patriarchate of Jerusalem</a></b> (<i>Patriarch of the Holy City of Jerusalem and all Holy Land, Syria, Arabia, beyond the Jordan River, Cana of Galilee, and Sacred Zion</i>)\n<ul><li>Autonomous <a href="/wiki/Saint_Catherine%27s_Monastery" title="Saint Catherine&#39;s Monastery">Church of Mount Sinai</a> (<i>Archbishop of Choreb, Sinai, and Raitha</i>)</li></ul></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Patriarchate of Russia</a></b> (<i>Patriarch of Moscow and all Russia</i>)\n<ul><li>Autonomous <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Orthodox_Church" title="Japanese Orthodox Church">Orthodox Church in Japan</a> (<i>Archbishop of Tokyo and Metropolitan of All Japan</i>)</li>\n<li>Autonomous <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Orthodox_Church" title="Chinese Orthodox Church">Orthodox Church of China</a> (<i>defunct</i>)</li>\n<li>Exarchate of <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_Orthodox_Church" title="Belarusian Orthodox Church">Belarus</a> (<i>Metropolitan of Minsk and Slutsk, Patriarchal Exarch of All Belarus</i>)</li>\n<li>Self-governing <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church_Outside_Russia" title="Russian Orthodox Church Outside Russia">Russian Orthodox Church Outside Russia</a> (<i>Metropolitan of Eastern America and New York, First Hierarch of the Russian church abroad</i>)</li>\n<li>Self-governing <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Orthodox_Church_(Moscow_Patriarchate)" title="Ukrainian Orthodox Church (Moscow Patriarchate)">Orthodox Church of Ukraine</a> (<i>Metropolitan of Kiev and all Ukraine</i>)</li>\n<li>Self-governing <a href="/wiki/Metropolis_of_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_and_All_Moldova" title="Metropolis of Chi\xc8\x99in\xc4\x83u and All Moldova">Orthodox Church of Moldova</a> (<i>Metropolitan of Chi\xc5\x9fin\xc4\x83u and all Moldova</i>)</li>\n<li>Self-governing <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Orthodox_Church" title="Latvian Orthodox Church">Orthodox Church of Latvia</a> (<i>Metropolitan of Riga and all Latvia</i>)</li>\n<li>Self-governing <a href="/wiki/Estonian_Orthodox_Church_of_Moscow_Patriarchate" title="Estonian Orthodox Church of Moscow Patriarchate">Estonian Orthodox Church of Moscow Patriarchate</a> (<i>Metropolitan of Tallinn and all Estonia</i>) [Autonomy not recognised by the Ecumenical Patriarchate]</li></ul></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">Serbian Patriarchate</a></b> (<i>Archbishop of Pe\xc4\x87, Metropolitan of Belgrade and Karlovci, and Serbian Patriarch</i>)\n<ul><li>Autonomous <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Ohrid_Archbishopric" title="Orthodox Ohrid Archbishopric">Orthodox Ohrid Archbishopric</a> (<i>Archbishop of Ohrid and Metropolitan of Skopje</i>)</li></ul></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Orthodox_Church" title="Bulgarian Orthodox Church">Patriarchate of Bulgaria</a></b> (<i>Metropolitan of Sofia and Patriarch of All Bulgaria</i>)</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Romanian_Orthodox_Church" title="Romanian Orthodox Church">Patriarchate of Romania</a></b> (<i>Archbishop of Bucharest, Metropolitan of Muntenia and Dobrudja, and Patriarch of All Romania</i>)</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Georgian_Orthodox_Church" title="Georgian Orthodox Church">Patriarchate of Georgia</a></b> (<i>Catholicos-Patriarch of All Georgia, the Archbishop of Mtskheta-Tbilisi and Metropolitan bishop of Abkhazia and Pitsunda.</i>)</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Church_of_Greece" title="Church of Greece">Church of Greece</a></b> (<i>Archbishop of Athens and all Greece</i>)</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Church_of_Cyprus" title="Church of Cyprus">Church of Cyprus</a></b> (<i>Archbishop of New Justiniana and all Cyprus</i>)</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Albanian_Orthodox_Church" title="Albanian Orthodox Church">Orthodox Church of Albania</a></b> (<i>Archbishop of Tirana, Durres and all Albania</i>)</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church_in_America" title="Orthodox Church in America">Orthodox Church in America</a></b> (<i>Archbishop of Washington, Metropolitan of All America and Canada</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;e&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Czech_and_Slovak_Orthodox_Church" title="Czech and Slovak Orthodox Church">Orthodox Church of the Czech lands and Slovakia</a></b> (<i>Archbishop of Prague, the Metropolitan of Czech lands and Slovakia or the Archbishop of Presov, the Metropolitan of Czech lands and Slovakia</i>)</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Polish_Orthodox_Church" title="Polish Orthodox Church">Orthodox Church of Poland</a></b> (<i>Metropolitan of Warsaw and all Poland</i>)</li></ul>\n<p>There are unresolved internal issues as to the autonomous or autocephalous status of the following Orthodox churches:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Estonian_Apostolic_Orthodox_Church" title="Estonian Apostolic Orthodox Church">Estonian Apostolic Orthodox Church</a> (<i>Metropolitan of Tallinn and all Estonia</i>) \xe2\x80\x94 Autonomy is recognised only by the Ecumenical Patriarchate, opposed only by the Russian Orthodox Church</li>\n<li>Self-governing <a href="/wiki/Metropolis_of_Bessarabia" title="Metropolis of Bessarabia">Metropolis of Bessarabia</a> of the Romanian Orthodox Church \xe2\x80\x94 Autonomy is objected by the Russian Orthodox Church</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditionalist_groups">Traditionalist groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Traditionalist groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Crucession_Davidovo-Elizarovo_Guslitci_Moscow_reg_8504.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Crucession_Davidovo-Elizarovo_Guslitci_Moscow_reg_8504.jpg/250px-Crucession_Davidovo-Elizarovo_Guslitci_Moscow_reg_8504.jpg" width="250" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Crucession_Davidovo-Elizarovo_Guslitci_Moscow_reg_8504.jpg/375px-Crucession_Davidovo-Elizarovo_Guslitci_Moscow_reg_8504.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Crucession_Davidovo-Elizarovo_Guslitci_Moscow_reg_8504.jpg/500px-Crucession_Davidovo-Elizarovo_Guslitci_Moscow_reg_8504.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Crucession_Davidovo-Elizarovo_Guslitci_Moscow_reg_8504.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Traditional <a href="/wiki/Easter" title="Easter">Paschal</a> procession by Russian Orthodox Old-Rite Church</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/True_Orthodoxy" title="True Orthodoxy">True Orthodoxy</a> separated from the mainstream communion over issues of <a href="/wiki/Ecumenism" title="Ecumenism">ecumenism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Old_Calendarists" title="Old Calendarists">calendar reform</a> since the 1920s.<sup id="cite_ref-politika_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-politika-206">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> The movement rejects the <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarchate" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecumenical Patriarchate">Ecumenical Patriarchate</a> of Constantinople, the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Patriarchate" class="mw-redirect" title="Moscow Patriarchate">Moscow Patriarchate</a>, and those Churches in communion with them, accusing them of heresy and placing themselves under bishops who do the same. They adhere to the use of the old <a href="/wiki/Julian_Calendar" class="mw-redirect" title="Julian Calendar">Julian Calendar</a> since Antiquity, claiming that the <a href="/wiki/New_Calendarists" class="mw-redirect" title="New Calendarists">calendar reform</a> in 1920s is in contravention of the <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Councils" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecumenical Councils">Ecumenical Councils</a>. True Orthodox writers have argued that in missionary areas such as the United States, Orthodox (<a href="/wiki/SCOBA" class="mw-redirect" title="SCOBA">SCOBA</a>) membership numbers may be overstated, with the comparative number of True Orthodox as up to 15% of the Orthodox population, in Russia, it has been claimed by some clergy that up to a million Russians may be True Orthodox of different jurisdictions, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Christian_denominations_by_number_of_members" title="List of Christian denominations by number of members">though the total number is often cited at 1.7-2 million together.</a>\n</p><p>There is no official communion of traditionalists. They often are local groups and are limited to a specific bishop or locality. The following is a list:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Churches descending from the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church_Outside_Russia#Schism" title="Russian Orthodox Church Outside Russia">Russian Orthodox Church Outside Russia</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Greek_Old_Calendarists" title="Greek Old Calendarists">Greek Old Calendarists</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Old_Calendar_Bulgarian_Orthodox_Church" title="Old Calendar Bulgarian Orthodox Church">Old Calendar Bulgarian Orthodox Church</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Old_Calendar_Romanian_Orthodox_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Calendar Romanian Orthodox Church">Old Calendar Romanian Orthodox Church</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Autonomous_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Autonomous Church">Russian Orthodox Autonomous Church</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Serbian_True_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian True Orthodox Church">Serbian True Orthodox Church</a></li></ul>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Old_Believers" title="Old Believers">Old Believers</a> are groups that do not accept liturgical reforms carried out in the Russian Orthodox Church by Patriarch Nikon in the 17th century. Although all Old Believers groups emerged as a result of opposition to the Nikonian reform, they do not constitute a single monolithic body. Despite the emphasis on invariable adherence to the pre-Nikonian traditions, the Old Believers feature a great diversity of groups that profess different interpretations of the church tradition and often are not in communion with each other (some groups even practise re-baptism before admitting a member of another group into their midst).\n</p><p>Old Believers:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Old-Rite_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Old-Rite Church">Russian Orthodox Old-Rite Church</a> (<a href="/wiki/Belokrinitskaya_Hierarchy" title="Belokrinitskaya Hierarchy">Belokrinitskaya Hierarchy</a>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lipovan_Orthodox_Old-Rite_Church" title="Lipovan Orthodox Old-Rite Church">Lipovan Orthodox Old-Rite Church</a> (Belokrinitskaya Hierarchy)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Russian_Old-Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Old-Orthodox Church">Russian Old-Orthodox Church</a> (Novozybkovskaya Hierarchy)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pomorian_Old-Orthodox_Church" title="Pomorian Old-Orthodox Church">Pomorian Old-Orthodox Church</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pomortsy" class="mw-redirect" title="Pomortsy">Pomortsy</a>)</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Churches_not_in_communion_with_others">Churches not in communion with others</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Churches not in communion with others">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Churches with irregular or unresolved canonical status are entities that have carried out <a href="/wiki/Episcopi_vagantes" title="Episcopi vagantes">episcopal consecrations outside of the norms of canon law</a> or whose bishops have been excommunicated by one of the 14 (15) autocephalous churches. These include nationalist and other schisms.\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Abkhazian_Orthodox_Church" title="Abkhazian Orthodox Church">Abkhazian Orthodox Church</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Belarusian_Autocephalous_Orthodox_Church" title="Belarusian Autocephalous Orthodox Church">Belarusian Autocephalous Orthodox Church</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Communion_of_the_Western_Orthodox_Churches" class="mw-redirect" title="Communion of the Western Orthodox Churches">Communion of the Western Orthodox Churches</a> (<a href="/wiki/Celtic_Orthodox_Church" title="Celtic Orthodox Church">Celtic Orthodox Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church_of_France" title="Orthodox Church of France">French Orthodox Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church_of_the_Gauls" title="Orthodox Church of the Gauls">Orthodox Church of the Gauls</a>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Croatian_Orthodox_Church" title="Croatian Orthodox Church">Croatian Orthodox Church</a>, existed 1942-45</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Orthodox_Church" title="Evangelical Orthodox Church">Evangelical Orthodox Church</a>, only Eastern Orthodox denomination that mixes with Charismatic and Evangelical elements.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Holy_Orthodox_Church_in_North_America" title="Holy Orthodox Church in North America">Holy Orthodox Church in North America</a>, in communion with Greek Old Calendarists</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lusitanian_Orthodox_Church" title="Lusitanian Orthodox Church">Lusitanian Orthodox Church</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Macedonian_Orthodox_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Macedonian Orthodox Church">Macedonian Orthodox Church</a> \xe2\x80\x93 The Church proclaimed independence, but this is objected by the Serbian Orthodox Church as a schism. Though officially unrecognised by the other churches in the communion, the Macedonian Orthodox Church de facto communicates with many of the churches.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Montenegrin_Orthodox_Church" title="Montenegrin Orthodox Church">Montenegrin Orthodox Church</a>, in full communion with the Ukrainian Orthodox Kiev Patriarchate</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church_in_Italy" title="Orthodox Church in Italy">Orthodox Church in Italy</a>, since 2013 a vicariate of the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Catholic_Church" title="Nordic Catholic Church">Nordic Catholic Church</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Old_Catholic_Church_in_Italy" title="Old Catholic Church in Italy">Old Catholic Church in Italy</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church_of_Greece_(Holy_Synod_in_Resistance)" title="Orthodox Church of Greece (Holy Synod in Resistance)">Orthodox Church of Greece (Holy Synod in Resistance)</a> (as of 2014 in communion with Greek Old Calendarists)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Russian_True_Orthodox_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian True Orthodox Church">Russian True Orthodox Church</a> aka Catacomb Church</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/True_Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="True Russian Orthodox Church">True Russian Orthodox Church</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Turkish_Orthodox_Patriarchate" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Orthodox Patriarchate">Turkish Orthodox Church</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Orthodox_Church_(Kiev_Patriarchate)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukrainian Orthodox Church (Kiev Patriarchate)">Ukrainian Orthodox Church (Kiev Patriarchate)</a>, in full communion with the Montenegrin Orthodox Church</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Autocephalous_Orthodox_Church" title="Ukrainian Autocephalous Orthodox Church">Ukrainian Autocephalous Orthodox Church</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Autocephalous_Orthodox_Church_Canonical" title="Ukrainian Autocephalous Orthodox Church Canonical">Ukrainian Autocephalous Orthodox Church Canonical</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span Catholic Church and the Eastern Orthodox Church">Theological differences between the Catholic Church and the Eastern Orthodox Church</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Orthodoxy_in_Greece_(33-717)" class="mw-redirect" title="Timeline of Orthodoxy in Greece (33-717)">Timeline of Orthodoxy in Greece (33-717)</a></li></ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes_and_references">Notes and references</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Notes and references">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-67"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-67">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to Roman Lunkin in an interview about the 2012 survey published by <span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">\xd0\xa1\xd1\x80\xd0\xb5\xd0\xb4\xd0\xb0</span> (<i><i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian-language transliteration">Sreda</i></i>), about 40% of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a> population is Orthodox. However, only 5% belong to a parish or regularly attend Divine Liturgy. Lunkin said that this was long known by experts but a myth persists that 80\xe2\x80\x9390% of the population is Orthodox.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> According to <i>The World Factbook</i> 2006 estimate, 15\xe2\x80\x9320% are practicing Russian Orthodox but there is a large populations of non-practicing believers.<sup id="cite_ref-CIAWeb_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIAWeb-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-70"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-70">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Data is estimated, there are no census figures available, Greece is said to be 98% Orthodox by CIA, but additional studies found only 60-80% believe in God, if true, then no more than 80% may be Orthodox.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-85"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-85">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to Alexei Krindatch, "the total number of Orthodox parishes" increased by 16% from 2000 to 2010 in the United States, from this, he wrote that Orthodox Churches are growing.<sup id="cite_ref-Krindatch2010_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krindatch2010-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">(<span>p2</span>)</sup> Krindatch did not provide figures about any change in the membership over that same period in his 2010 highlight.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-88">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to Oliver Herbel, in <i>Turning to Tradition</i>, the 2008 US Religious Landscape Survey "suggests that if there is growth, it is statistically insignificant."<sup id="cite_ref-Herbel2014_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Herbel2014-86">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">(<span>p9</span>)</sup> The 2014 US Religious Landscape Survey also shows, within the survey\'s \xc2\xb19.2% margin of sampling error corresponding to the sample size of the <i>Orthodox Christian</i> category being 186 people, a statistically insignificant decline within the category "Orthodox Christians" as the percentage of population from 2007 to 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-PewRLS2015_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PewRLS2015-87">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">(<span>pp4, 21, 36, 93</span>)</sup> But only 53% of people who were Orthodox Christian as children still self identify as Orthodox Christian in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-PewRLS2015_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PewRLS2015-87">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">(<span>p39</span>)</sup> The <i>Orthodox Christian</i> category "is most heavily made up of immigrants and the children of immigrants."<sup id="cite_ref-PewRLS2015_87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PewRLS2015-87">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">(<span>p53</span>)</sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-205"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-205">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Autocephaly was granted in 1970 from its mother church, the Russian Orthodox Church. No church has yet objected the inclusion of the Orthodox Church in America. It is in full communion with all canonical Orthodox churches and therefore fully recognised by all <i>de facto</i>. Upon gaining autocephaly it became the 15th church within the communion. The Ecumenical Patriarchate accepts the Orthodox Church in America, but disputes the Russian Orthodox Church\'s action of granting autocephaly. There are no Orthodox canons stating who can or cannot grant autocephaly.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eastern_Orthodox_Church&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-brit-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-brit_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-brit_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-brit_1-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Meyendorff, John (2014-07-14). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.britannica.com/topic/Eastern-Orthodoxy#toc59581">"Eastern Orthodoxy"</a>. <i>britannica.com</i>. the historical links of the Orthodox Catholic church with the Eastern Roman Empire and Byzantium (Constantinople), however, the <a href="/wiki/Exonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Exonym">exonyms</a> in American English usage referred to it as the "Eastern" or "Greek Orthodox" Church. Penguin Adult. p.&#160;322. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780140146561" title="Special:BookSources/9780140146561">9780140146561</a>. <q>From the beginning of the twentieth century the Ecumenical Patriarchate has shown a special concern for Christian reconciliation. At his accession in 1902, Patriarch Joachim III sent an encyclical letter to all the autocephalous Orthodox Churches, asking in particular for their opinion on relations with other Christian bodies. In January 1920 the Ecumenical Patriarchate followed this up with a bold and prophetic letter addressed \'To all the Churches of Christ, wherever they may be\', urging closer co-operation among separated Christians, and suggesting a \'League of Churches\', parallel to the newly founded League of Nations. Many of the ideas in this letter anticipate subsequent developments in the WCC. Constantinople, along with several of the other Orthodox Churches, was represented at the Faith and Order Conferences at Lausanne in 1927 and at Edinburgh in 1937. The Ecumenical Patriarchate also participated in the first Assembly of the WCC at Amsterdam in 1948, and has been a consistent supporter of the work of the WCC ever since.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Orthodox+Church&amp;rft.pages=322&amp;rft.pub=Penguin+Adult&amp;rft.date=1993-04-29&amp;rft.isbn=9780140146561&amp;rft.aulast=Ware&amp;rft.aufirst=Kallistos&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEastern+Orthodox+Church" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Fuchs2008-192"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Fuchs2008_192-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Fuchs, Lorelei F.
